            if (typeof (gptText) == "string") {
                gptText = gptText.replace(/\&/g, '%26');
                return gptText.replace(/\^|\*|#|\$|\"|\'|\=|\,|\!|\+|\~|\;|\(|\)|\<|\>|\[|\]|\?|\%|\:|\@|\;|\&|\||\{|\}|\\|/g, '');
            }
            return "blank";
        }

        googletag.pubads()
            .setTargeting('property', 'value-of-property')    // Change and duplicate this line for as many additional keywords to send
            .setTargeting('doi', gptClean('10.1002/adma.202211690')) // Publication DOI
            .setTargeting('pbPage', gptClean(gptPage))
            .setTargeting('pbSubPage', gptClean(gptSubPage))
            .setTargeting('urlpath', gptClean(document.location.pathname));

        googletag.defineSlot($GooglePublisherCategory, 'fluid', 'advert-leaderboard')
            .defineSizeMapping(sizes.leaderboard)

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/templates/jsp/pb2/js/plugin/thiss-ds.js" nonce="645e6734a49b4ac0a9411bc06980716e"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="645e6734a49b4ac0a9411bc06980716e">

        function getParameter(parameterName) {
            let result = null,
                tmp = [];
            location.search
                .substr(1)
                .split("&")
                .forEach(function (item) {
                    tmp = item.split("=");
                    if (tmp[0] === parameterName) result = tmp[1];
                });
            return result;
        }

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            queryParamsDelimiter: encodeURIComponent('?'),

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                let redirectURL = getParameter('redirectUri');
                if(redirectURL == null){
                    redirectURL = encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
                }
                if(redirectURL.indexOf('saml_referrer') < 0){
                    redirectURL += encodeURIComponent(((redirectURL.indexOf(this.queryParamsDelimiter) !== -1) ? '&' : '?') + 'saml_referrer');
                }
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + redirectURL;
            },
            retrieveEntity: function () {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // get the results
                            var results = res.data;
                            return resolve(results);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('retrieve entity error: ' + err);
                        });
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage duo to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {doi: doi, entityid: entityId, entityTitle: entityTitle, eventGroupKey: '3d882adb-6101-42a9-ac38-c5c67a382cc0'}

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (let i in allSsoInstitutions) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();
                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err){
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

        (function() {
            function riskifiedBeaconLoad() {
                var store_domain = 'https://advanced.onlinelibrary.wiley.com';
                var session_id = '7D80A9C81A4E65BFABF55E3344614FAA';
                var url = ('https:' == document.location.protocol ? 'https://' : 'http://')
                    + "beacon.riskified.com?shop=" + store_domain + "&sid=" + session_id;
                var s = document.createElement('script');
                s.type = 'text/javascript';
                s.async = true;
                s.src = url;
                var x = document.getElementsByTagName('script')[0];
                x.parentNode.insertBefore(s, x);
            }
            if (window.attachEvent)
                window.attachEvent('onload', riskifiedBeaconLoad)
            else
                window.addEventListener('load', riskifiedBeaconLoad, false);
        })();

China</p><a class="moreInfoLink" href="/authored-by/Wang/Peng">Search for more papers by this author</a></div></span><span class="accordion-tabbed__tab-mobile  accordion__closed"><a href="/authored-by/Li/Hui" class="author-name accordion-tabbed__control" data-id="a7" data-db-target-for="a7" aria-controls="a7" aria-haspopup="true" id="a7_Ctrl" role="button"><span>Hui Li</span><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-section_arrow_d"></i></a><span class="comma-separator">,&nbsp;</span><div class="author-info accordion-tabbed__content" data-db-target-of="a7" aria-labelledby="a7_Ctrl" role="region" id="a7">

   <div class="abstract-group ">
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" lang="en" data-lang="en" lang-name="English" id="section-1-en">
         <h2 id="d21120041" class="article-section__header section__title main abstractlang_en main">Abstract</h2>
         <div class="article-section__content en main">
            
            <p>2D transition metal dichalcogenides (TMDCs) and single-atom catalysts (SACs) are promising electrodes for energy conversion/storage because of the layered structure and maximum atom utilization efficiency. However, the integration of such two type materials and the relevant sodium storage applications remain daunting challenges. Here, an ingenious diatomite-templated synthetic strategy is designed to fabricate single-atom cobalt-doped MoS<sub>2</sub>/carbon (SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C) composites toward the high-performance sodium storage. Benefiting from the unique hierarchical structure, high electron/sodium-ion conductivity, and abundant active sites, the obtained SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C reveals remarkable specific capacity (≈604.0 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup>), high rate performance, and outstanding long cyclic stability. Particularly, the sodium-ion full cell composed of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C anode and Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> cathode demonstrates unexpected stability with the cycle number exceeded 1200. The internal sodium storage mechanism is clarified with the aid of density functional theory calculations and in situ experimental characterizations. This work not only represents a substantial leap in terms of synthesizing SACs on 2D TMDCs but also provides a crucial step toward the practical sodium-ion battery applications.</p>
            </div>
      </section>
   </div>
   <div class="pb-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="below-abstract-group"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div>
   
   <section class="article-section article-section__full">
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adma202211690-sec-0010">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adma202211690-sec-0010-title">1 Introduction</h2>
         
         <p>Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are identified as appealing alternatives to lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), especially in the grid-scale energy storage because of the abundant source and low cost of sodium, as well as the feasibility for large-scale production using the existing infrastructure of LIBs.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211690-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0001_R_d21120032e491" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Nat. Rev. Mater.">1</a>-<a href="#adma202211690-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0008_R_d21120032e491" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - ACS Nano">8</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, compared to lithium ion (≈0.59 Å), the larger diameter (≈0.99 Å) of sodium ion limits the exploitation of suitable anodes and also results in the sluggish reaction kinetics.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211690-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0009_R_d21120032e496" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Acc. Chem. Res.">9</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Designing promising electrodes with long cyclic stability and high rate capability is becoming the most pivotal task to address this issue, and many efforts have been devoted, including the introduction of 2D materials, such as graphene,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211690-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0010_R_d21120032e501" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - Science">10</a>, <a href="#adma202211690-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0011_R_d21120032e501" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Nat. Nanotechnol.">11</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> transition metal dichalcogenides (TMDCs),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211690-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0012_R_d21120032e507" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - Nat. Commun.">12</a>, <a href="#adma202211690-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0013_R_d21120032e507" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Nat. Commun.">13</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and MXenes.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211690-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0014_R_d21120032e512" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Nat. Rev. Mater.">14</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Thereinto, the layered MoS<sub>2</sub> is a desirable anode for sodium storage in view of its large interlayer space and high theoretical capacity.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211690-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0015_R_d21120032e520" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - Sci. Adv.">15</a>-<a href="#adma202211690-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0017_R_d21120032e520" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - Adv. Energy Mater.">17</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Nevertheless, the low conductivity, limited active sites, insufficient charge/mass transfer, and considerable volume variation greatly deteriorate the SIB performances.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211690-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0018_R_d21120032e525" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Nat. Commun.">18</a>, <a href="#adma202211690-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0019_R_d21120032e525" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - Adv. Mater.">19</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>Single-atom catalysts (SACs) featured with single atoms dispersed on different matrices have attracted considerable attention in field of heterogenous catalysis.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211690-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0020_R_d21120032e532" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Nat. Chem.">20</a>-<a href="#adma202211690-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0024_R_d21120032e532" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Adv. Mater.">24</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Apart from the maximum atom utilization efficiency, SACs possess high intrinsic activity, flexible selectivity, and low cost, which contribute to enhance the battery performances. For example, Zn single atoms were introduced into the hollow carbon spheres to modulate the chemical coordination environment and increase the potassium storage efficiency.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211690-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0025_R_d21120032e537" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - Matter">25</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Co single atoms were synthesized on N-doped hollow porous carbon, and were used as the cathodes of lithium-selenium batteries to activate selenium reactivity and immobilize polyselenides.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211690-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0026_R_d21120032e542" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - Nat. Commun.">26</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The unique double-end binding sites were achieved in a highly oriented microporous frame by integrating ZnS nanoparticles and Co-N-C single atoms, which effectively immobilized and converted the polysulfide intermediates during the cycling processes of lithium-sulfur battery.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211690-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0027_R_d21120032e548" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Nat. Nanotechnol.">27</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Unsaturated Fe single atoms were crafted on hierarchical C<sub>3</sub>N<sub>4</sub> architectures by means of biotemplated synthesis method, which delivered highly electrocatalytic activity to improve the dual-directional sulfur redox capacity.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211690-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0028_R_d21120032e558" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - Adv. Mater.">28</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Even so, the mediocre loading capacity, inferior atom utilization, and elusive catalytic pathway handicap the practical applications of SACs.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211690-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0029_R_d21120032e563" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Nat. Nanotechnol.">29</a>, <a href="#adma202211690-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0030_R_d21120032e563" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - Nat. Synth.">30</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In addition, the secondary battery applications of single-atom doped TMDCs are still unaddressed. Notably, Fe single atom doped N-doped graphene@MoS<sub>2</sub><sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211690-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0031_R_d21120032e569" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - Adv. Mater.">31</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and Sn nanoparticle/MoS<sub>2</sub>@C<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211690-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0032_R_d21120032e577" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - ACS Nano">32</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> have been synthesized and then used as the high-performance anodes of SIBs.</p>
         
         <p>To tackle such issues, we develop a high-throughput synthetic strategy to produce single-atom cobalt-doped MoS<sub>2</sub>/carbon (SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C) composites using the naturally abundant diatomite as the template. The superiorities of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C as the anodes of SIBs can be summarized as follows: 1) the unique biomorphic structure of diatomite provides a plentiful of anchoring sites to synthesize high loading of Co single atoms; 2) the Co doping modifies the electronic structure of MoS<sub>2</sub>, increases the conductivity, and facilitates the migration of Na atoms; 3) the hierarchical framework and adequate porosity of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C contribute to stabilize the structure and buffer the volume expansion during the charging/discharging processes. As expected, the remarkable specific capacity, good rate performance, and excellent long cyclic stability are achieved in SIBs composed of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C anodes. This work provides a new route for designing highly active and stable anodes of SIBs by introducing SACs on 2D TMDCs.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adma202211690-sec-0020">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adma202211690-sec-0020-title">2 Results and Discussion</h2>
         
         <p>The anode with hierarchical structure to enable high rate performance and volume change accommodation is highly desirable for LIBs and SIBs.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211690-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0013_R_d21120032e607" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Nat. Commun.">13</a>, <a href="#adma202211690-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0033_R_d21120032e607" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - Nat. Commun.">33</a>, <a href="#adma202211690-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0034_R_d21120032e607" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - Nat. Commun.">34</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The diatomite is selected as the growth template of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C because of its high natural abundance, low cost, and enough pore space to accommodate sufficient product inside.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211690-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0028_R_d21120032e614" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - Adv. Mater.">28</a>, <a href="#adma202211690-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0035_R_d21120032e614" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - Nat. Commun.">35</a>-<a href="#adma202211690-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0037_R_d21120032e614" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - ACS Nano">37</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Notably, the conformal coating of active material inherits the hierarchical morphology of diatomite, thereby endowing the obtained SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C composites with versatile pore structures and abundant active sites. The synthesis processes of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C composites are illustrated in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adma202211690-fig-0001">1</a>, and C<sub>3</sub>H<sub>3</sub>N<sub>3</sub>S<sub>3</sub>, H<sub>3</sub>[P(Mo<sub>3</sub>O<sub>10</sub>)]<sub>4</sub>, Co(NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>2</sub>, and C<sub>6</sub>H<sub>5</sub>Na<sub>3</sub>O<sub>7</sub> are used as the precursors.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adma202211690-fig-0001"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/37b62655-b8ec-439b-89cd-2c54470c34d3/adma202211690-fig-0001-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/37b62655-b8ec-439b-89cd-2c54470c34d3/adma202211690-fig-0001-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/922536b8-89ce-4813-937b-80e2d6475b20/adma202211690-fig-0001-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/37b62655-b8ec-439b-89cd-2c54470c34d3/adma202211690-fig-0001-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 1<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma202211690-fig-0001&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.202211690" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Schematic illustration of the synthesis processes of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C composites with naturally abundant diatomite as the template.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>Scanning electron microscopy (SEM) measurements were performed to characterize the morphologies of obtained samples. 3D disc-like diatomite is observed featured with uniform pores, which contribute to the batch synthesis of 2D materials (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#adma202211690-fig-0002">2a</a>). Notably, the fine hierarchical structure of diatomite can be preserved during the synthesis processes and further inherited by the derived SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and MoS<sub>2</sub>/C composites, as revealed in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0002">2b,c</a>. Such a unique structure is beneficial for facilitating the mass transport and accessibility of active sites during the electrochemical processes. The thickness of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C is determined to be ≈4.0&nbsp;nm, comparable with that of MoS<sub>2</sub>/C (≈4.1&nbsp;nm), indicative of their 2D features (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>, Supporting Information). By virtue of the hierarchical structure, relatively high specific surface areas of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C (≈94.5 m<sup>2</sup> g<sup>−1</sup>) and MoS<sub>2</sub>/C (≈94.1 m<sup>2</sup> g<sup>−1</sup>) are confirmed by the nitrogen adsorption/desorption isotherms, as shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a> (Supporting Information). X-ray diffraction (XRD) characterizations were then carried out on as-grown SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and MoS<sub>2</sub>/C to analyze their crystalline structures and phase states (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0002">2d</a>). The robust atomic structure of 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> is convinced by the unchanged diffraction peak positions after introducing Co. Particularly, the characteristic peaks of Co clusters are not detected, tentative indicating that Co atoms are exist in an atomically dispersed form. Furthermore, the carbon contents of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and MoS<sub>2</sub>/C are assessed to be ≈31.8% and ≈30.8%, respectively (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a>, Supporting Information). Such results suggest that the morphology, thickness, and phase state of MoS<sub>2</sub> are reserved after Co doping.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adma202211690-fig-0002"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/6b1b3387-8deb-4a88-ac57-4e720832b06a/adma202211690-fig-0002-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/6b1b3387-8deb-4a88-ac57-4e720832b06a/adma202211690-fig-0002-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/2252a4b9-7d38-4a1c-9c40-9a444a81d33d/adma202211690-fig-0002-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/6b1b3387-8deb-4a88-ac57-4e720832b06a/adma202211690-fig-0002-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 2<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma202211690-fig-0002&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.202211690" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Multiscale characterizations of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and MoS<sub>2</sub>/C. a–c) SEM images of diatomite, MoS<sub>2</sub>/C, and SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C, respectively. The hierarchical structure of diatomite is inherited by SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and MoS<sub>2</sub>/C. d) XRD patterns of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and MoS<sub>2</sub>/C. The characteristic peaks of Co clusters are not observed, indicative of the atomic dispersion of Co on MoS<sub>2</sub>. e) Raman spectra of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and MoS<sub>2</sub>/C. f) XPS spectra of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and MoS<sub>2</sub>/C. The blueshifts of Mo 3d and S 2p peaks for SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C indicate that the Co doping modifies the redox states of Mo and S.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>To further explore the effect of Co doping on the electronic structure and optical property of MoS<sub>2</sub>, Raman and X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) measurements were thus performed on as-grown samples. As displayed in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0002">2e</a>, two typical Raman characteristic peaks of 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> are observed for SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and MoS<sub>2</sub>/C. Nevertheless, the signal of 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> is not detected, suggesting that the phase transition is not occurred even after introducing Co atoms. Notably, the distinct redshifts of A<sub>1g</sub> and E<sup>1</sup> <sub>2</sub><sub>g</sub> modes are discovered for SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C (≈379.2 and ≈403.5 cm<sup>−1</sup>) comparing with those of MoS<sub>2</sub>/C (≈382.6 and ≈405.2 cm<sup>−1</sup>), possibly due to the n-doping effect and tensile strain from Co atoms, and a similar phenomenon is also demonstrated in Co-doped MoS<sub>2</sub> nanosheets.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211690-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0038_R_d21120032e825" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">38</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The prominent peaks at ≈1362.0 and ≈1587.0 cm<sup>−1</sup> are attributed to D and G bands of graphitic carbon, respectively. XPS characterizations were then employed to determine the electronic structures and chemical compositions of products (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0002">2f</a> and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a>, Supporting Information). The high-resolution Mo 3<i>d</i> and S 2<i>p</i> spectra of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and MoS<sub>2</sub>/C are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0002">2f</a>, respectively. For MoS<sub>2</sub>/C, the binding energies at ≈232.0 and ≈228.8&nbsp;eV are attributed to Mo<sup>4+</sup>, while ≈162.9 and ≈161.7&nbsp;eV are assigned to S<sup>2−</sup>. However, the characteristic peaks of Mo 3<i>d</i> (≈231.9 and ≈228.7&nbsp;eV) and S 2<i>p</i> (≈162.8 and 161.6&nbsp;eV) of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C show obviously shift to low binding energies. Such results substantiate the presence of electronic interaction between MoS<sub>2</sub> and Co, signifying the formation of coupled MoS<sub>2</sub>/Co interfaces. It is worth noting that the signal of Co<sup>0</sup> at ≈778.3&nbsp;eV is not observed, which further excludes the formation of Co clusters (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a>, Supporting Information). In short, SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C composites have been synthesized using diatomite as the template, the electronic structure renormalization and abundant active sites provide a platform for exploring multifunctional electrochemical energy storage applications.</p>
         
         <p>To scrutinize the chemical state and coordination environment of Co shell at atomic level, X-ray absorption fine structure (XAFS) measurements were then performed on as-grown samples. <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adma202211690-fig-0003">3a</a> reveals the Co <i>K</i>-edge X-ray absorption near-edge structure (XANES) spectra of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C, CoS, CoO, and commercial Co foil, respectively. The absorption edge of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C is situated between those of Co foil and CoO, and much closer to that of CoS, manifesting that the oxidation state of isolate Co atom in SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C is between Co<sup>0</sup> and Co<sup>2+</sup>. The quantitative structural information of Co can be readily documented by Fourier-transformed of extended X-ray absorption fine structure (FT-EXAFS) curves. As presented in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0003">3b</a>, SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C shows a dominant peak at ≈1.79 Å ascribed to Co<span class="icomoon"></span>S scattering path, which is also observed in CoS. This result indicates that the positively charged Co<i><sup><i>δ</i></sup></i><sup>+</sup> is stabilized by S atom in MoS<sub>2</sub>, consistent with the XPS results. In addition, the Co<span class="icomoon"></span>Co bond (≈2.18 Å) is absent for SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C, confirming the evolution of Co single atoms on MoS<sub>2</sub>. The wavelet transform (WT) EXAFS analyses with powerful resolution were also performed in <i>k</i> and <i>R</i> spaces, with the results shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0003">3c,d</a> and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6</a> (Supporting Information), respectively. The contour plot of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C displays a WT-maximum at ≈1.75 Å, corresponding to the Co<span class="icomoon"></span>S configuration, nevertheless, the WT-maximum of Co<span class="icomoon"></span>Co is not identified, reconfirming the formation of Co single atoms. The detailed EXAFS fitting structural parameters of Co <i>K</i>-edge are shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7</a> and Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a> (Supporting Information), respectively.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adma202211690-fig-0003"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/3bdffc94-0fc9-4edd-8cc2-5f125a702b95/adma202211690-fig-0003-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/3bdffc94-0fc9-4edd-8cc2-5f125a702b95/adma202211690-fig-0003-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/a8ad2fa2-7ae4-40cc-a2e6-4c26cc6b2758/adma202211690-fig-0003-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/3bdffc94-0fc9-4edd-8cc2-5f125a702b95/adma202211690-fig-0003-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 3<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma202211690-fig-0003&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.202211690" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">The determination of Co single atom. a,b) XANES and FE-EXAFS spectra of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C, CoS, CoO, and commercial Co foil, respectively. c,d) WT contour plots at the Co K-edge of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and commercial Co foil. e) Low-magnification TEM image of transferred SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C. f) Corresponding atomic resolution HAADF-STEM image. The bright spots (marked with white circles) are identified to be Co single atoms. g) Low-magnification HAADF-STEM image of transferred SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C. h–k) Corresponding elemental maps of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>The atomic structure, crystalline quality, and the distribution of Co single atoms were further investigated by transmission electron microscopy (TEM) and high-angle annular dark-field scanning transmission electron microscopy (HAADF-STEM). Low-magnification TEM images of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and MoS<sub>2</sub>/C are presented in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0003">3e</a> and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8</a> (Supporting Information), respectively, where the ultrathin characteristics and hierarchical structures with abundant channels are observed. The atomic resolution HAADF-STEM image in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0003">3f</a> shows a perfect honeycomb lattice, indicative of the high crystalline quality of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C. In addition, the atomic dispersion of Co is also substantiated by the individual bright dots (marked with white circles), which are corresponding to the isolated single Co atoms (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0003">3f</a> and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S9</a>, Supporting Information). Energy dispersive spectroscopy (EDS) maps of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C reveal the homogeneous distribution of Co, Mo, S, and C elements (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0003">3g–k</a>). The inductively coupled plasma mass spectrometry (ICP-MS) analysis results indicate that the weight fraction of Co single atom in SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C is ≈3.35 wt% (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a>, Supporting Information). Notably, the doping concentration of Co single atom can be accurately controlled, as the amount of Co precursors is reduced to be ≈75&nbsp;mg, the weight fraction of Co single atom is calculated to be ≈2.62 wt% (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a>, Supporting Information). Such results suggest that the high density of Co single atoms have been successfully synthesized on MoS<sub>2</sub> by coordinating with S atoms.</p>
         
         <p>The electrochemical performances of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and MoS<sub>2</sub>/C composites were examined in sodium-ion half cells. <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adma202211690-fig-0004">4a</a> shows the cyclic voltammetry (CV) curves of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C for the initial three cycles at a scan rate of 0.2&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>. In the first cycle cathodic scan, two reduction peaks are observed at ≈0.70 and ≈0.38&nbsp;V, respectively, which are attributed to the intercalation of Na<sup>+</sup> ions and the formation of solid electrolyte interface (SEI) films, as well as the conversion reaction from Na<sub>x</sub>MoS<sub>2</sub> to Na<sub>2</sub>S/Mo. After the first anodic scan, a distinct peak is achieved at ≈1.82&nbsp;V for SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C, smaller than that of MoS<sub>2</sub>/C (≈1.84&nbsp;V), suggestive of the enhanced Na<sup>+</sup> extraction dynamics (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S10</a>, Supporting Information). The galvanostatic charging/discharging curves of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and MoS<sub>2</sub>/C for the first three cycles at the current density of 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup> are displayed in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0004">4b</a> and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11</a> (Supporting Information), respectively. In the first cycle, SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C delivers the discharging and charging specific capacities of ≈1078.0 and ≈593.0 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively, with the initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) of ≈55.0%. Notably, the large specific surface area of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and the introduction of carbon matrix induce the decomposition of electrolyte and the irreversible Na<sup>+</sup> ions trapping, which should result in the considerable side reaction and relatively low ICE. Even so, this value is still comparable to that of MoS<sub>2</sub><sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211690-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0039_R_d21120032e1067" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - Adv. Mater.">39</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and MoS<sub>2</sub>/SA Fe-N-C.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211690-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0040_R_d21120032e1074" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">40</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adma202211690-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/751839d7-39d0-440d-bd22-67906c677e32/adma202211690-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/751839d7-39d0-440d-bd22-67906c677e32/adma202211690-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/1a4b9e52-0f89-4b92-bf2a-b8a16de968cb/adma202211690-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/751839d7-39d0-440d-bd22-67906c677e32/adma202211690-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma202211690-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.202211690" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Electrochemical performances of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and MoS<sub>2</sub>/C. a) CV curves of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C in the first three cycles with a scan rate of 0.2&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>. b) Charging/discharging curves of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C in the first three cycles at the current density of 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup>. c) Rate capabilities of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and MoS<sub>2</sub>/C at different current densities. d,e) Cycling performances of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and MoS<sub>2</sub>/C at the current densities of 1 and 5 A g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. f) CV curves of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C at different scan rates. g) CV profile of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C with the capacitive contribution at a scan rate of 1.2&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>. h) Capacitive contributions at different scan rates for SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C. i) GITT potential profiles of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and MoS<sub>2</sub>/C. j,k) Na<sup>+</sup> ion diffusion coefficients of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and MoS<sub>2</sub>/C during the charging/discharging processes.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>The rate capabilities of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and MoS<sub>2</sub>/C were evaluated at different current densities (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0004">4c</a>). As the current density increases from 0.1 to 0.2 A g<sup>−1</sup>, the reversible capacities of ≈604.0 and ≈550.0 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> are obtained for SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C, much higher than those of MoS<sub>2</sub>/C (≈544.0 and ≈507.0 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>) and bare MoS<sub>2</sub> (≈498.0 and ≈437.0 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>) (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12</a>, Supporting Information). Interestingly, a reversible capacity of ≈323.0 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> is achieved even at the high current density of 5.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>, suggestive of the excellent rate capacity of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C. The cycling performances at different current densities were also explored to identify the stability of electrodes. SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub> possesses a reversible capacity of ≈449.0 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup> with the CE of ≈100%, and the capacity is maintained to be ≈427.0 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> even after 400 cycles, corresponding to a decay rate of ≈0.055% cycle<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0004">4d</a>). In contrast, MoS<sub>2</sub>/C displays a low reversible capacity of ≈244.0 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 400 cycles, accompanying with a high attenuation rate of ≈0.460% cycle<sup>−1</sup>. At an elevated current density of 5 A g<sup>−1</sup>, SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub> still presents a favorable cycling performance and the reversible capacity of ≈334.0 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> is maintained even after 1380 cycles, as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0004">4e</a>. Such results indicate that the introduction of Co single atom enhances the electrochemical performances of MoS<sub>2</sub>/C, including specific capacity, reaction kinetics, and cycling stability. The electrochemical performances of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C with different Co doping concentrations are shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13</a> (Supporting Information), where the highest sodium storage efficiency is obtained as the Co precursor is set to be 0.3&nbsp;mmol (the corresponding Co single atom doping concentration is determined to be ≈3.35%). The comparison of electrochemical performances for SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and MoS<sub>2</sub>/C with different mass loadings is revealed in Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S14 and S15</a> (Supporting Information). Meanwhile, the introduction of carbon should contribute to the intercalation and adsorption of Na<sup>+</sup> ions and then improve the sodium storage performances. The contrastive sodium-ion half-cell performances of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C with other MoS<sub>2</sub>-based electrodes are shown in Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a> (Supporting Information).</p>
         
         <div class="paragraph-element">To determine the capacitive contribution, CV curves of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and MoS<sub>2</sub>/C were examined at various scan rates from 0.2 to 1.2&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0004">4f</a>, and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S16a</a>, Supporting Information). The capacitive contribution can be calculated according to the equation of <i>i</i> = <i>k</i><sub>1</sub><i>ν</i> + <i>k</i><sub>2</sub><i>ν</i><sup>1/2</sup>, where <i>k</i><sub>1</sub><i>ν</i> and <i>k</i><sub>2</sub><i>ν</i><sup>1/2</sup> represent the capacitive contribution and ion diffusion, respectively. As depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0004">4g</a>, the capacitive contribution in SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C is obtained to be ≈97.0% at a scan rate of 1.2&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>. Notably, SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C displays higher capacitive contributions (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0004">4h</a>) than those of MoS<sub>2</sub>/C at different scan rates (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S16b,c</a>, Supporting Information), in consideration that the high conductivity of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub> facilitates the electron transfer.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211690-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0039_R_d21120032e1289" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - Adv. Mater.">39</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S17</a> (Supporting Information), the charge transfer resistances (before and after cycling test) are extracted from the electrochemical impedance spectra (EIS) of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>, much smaller than those of MoS<sub>2</sub>/C, confirming the fast charge transfer. To further explore the reaction kinetics of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and MoS<sub>2</sub>/C, the galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) measurements were then performed and the similar sodium storage mechanism of such two anodes are demonstrated (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0004">4i</a>). In addition, the Na<sup>+</sup> ion diffusion coefficient (<i>D</i><sub>Na+</sub>) is also calculated according to Fick's second law.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211690-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0016_R_d21120032e1315" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Adv. Mater.">16</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup><div class="inline-equation" id="adma202211690-disp-0001"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                  <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/23e3cebf-0000-4706-85ba-cc301378fd77/adma202211690-math-0001.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:09359648:media:adma202211690:adma202211690-math-0001" display="block" location="graphic/adma202211690-math-0001.png">

                        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}{D}_{{\rm{Na}}^ + } = \frac{4}{{\tau \pi }}{\left( {\frac{{{m}_{\rm{B}}{V}_{\rm{M}}}}{{{M}_{\rm{B}}S}}} \right)}^2{\left( {\frac{{\Delta {E}_{\rm{S}}}}{{\Delta {E}_{{\tau}}}}} \right)}^2\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                     </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(1)</span></div>where <i>τ</i>, <i>m</i><sub>B</sub>, <i>M</i><sub>B</sub>, <i>V</i><sub>M</sub>, and <i>S</i> are the time of current pulse, mass, molar mass, molar volume of active material, and area of electrode, respectively. Notably, SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C reveals much higher diffusion coefficient than that of MoS<sub>2</sub>/C during the discharging/charging processes, manifesting the improved Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0004">4j,k</a>).</div>
         
         <p>The sodium-ion half-cell composed of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub> anode is discharged from open-circuit voltage (OCP) to ≈0.01&nbsp;V and then charged from ≈0.01 to ≈3.0&nbsp;V, as described in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adma202211690-fig-0005">5a</a>. To identify the structure evolution, the in situ XRD measurements were performed on SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0005">5b,c</a>) and MoS<sub>2</sub>/C (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18</a>, Supporting Information). For SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C anode, the XRD characteristic peaks of MoS<sub>2</sub> at ≈33.5° ((100) plane) and ≈58.3° ((110) plane) are reappeared, suggesting the high structure stability. More importantly, the slight shift of the characteristic peak at ≈9.2° indicates the expanded interlayer spacing of MoS<sub>2</sub>, which should accommodate the volume expansion during the charging/discharging processes. For MoS<sub>2</sub>/C anode, the XRD characteristic peaks of MoS<sub>2</sub> are gradually weakened and then disappeared. Even charging to ≈3.0&nbsp;V, the characteristic peaks are still unrecovered, implying the irreversible structural evolution. Notably, the MoS<sub>2</sub> shows amorphous feature after charging to ≈3.0&nbsp;V, as confirmed by the HRTEM and SAED results in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19</a> (Supporting Information). To further analyze the structure evolution of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>, Raman characterizations were also employed, with the results shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S20</a> (Supporting Information). In detail, two Raman characteristic peaks gradually disappeared during the discharging processes, which suggests the complete decomposition of MoS<sub>2</sub>. Nevertheless, after charging to ≈2.1&nbsp;V, these two peaks are observed, manifesting the reappearance of MoS<sub>2</sub>.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adma202211690-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/2c5d6bf4-3df9-4c7e-a872-bc18986440bd/adma202211690-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/2c5d6bf4-3df9-4c7e-a872-bc18986440bd/adma202211690-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/136f5022-e5a7-47e5-b15c-a98c4f827ba0/adma202211690-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/2c5d6bf4-3df9-4c7e-a872-bc18986440bd/adma202211690-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma202211690-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.202211690" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">The sodium storage mechanism of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and MoS<sub>2</sub>/C. a) Charging/discharging curves of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C. b,c) In situ XRD patterns of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C during the charging/discharging processes. d–f) Atomic resolution HRTEM images of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C at different charging/discharging states. g) Electronic structures of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and MoS<sub>2</sub>/C. h) Migration energies of sodium atom on SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and MoS<sub>2</sub>/C. i) Atomic structures of the adsorbed sodium on SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub> and MoS<sub>2</sub>/C, as well as the corresponding isosurfaces of local charge density difference.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>HRTEM measurements were then carried out to visualize the atomic structure evolution of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>. After discharging to ≈2.1&nbsp;V, the lattice spacing of ≈0.23&nbsp;nm for MoS<sub>2</sub> is detected, as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0005">5d</a>. However, at the end of discharging process, Na<sub>2</sub>S is obtained with the interplanar space of ≈0.24&nbsp;nm (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0005">5e</a>). Interestingly, after charging to ≈3.0&nbsp;V, MoS<sub>2</sub> reappeared to show a lattice fringe of ≈0.23&nbsp;nm, highly indicative of its extraordinary structure stability (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0005">5f</a>). In addition, after 70 cycles, Co single atoms are still observed, reconfirming the excellent stability of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S21</a>, Supporting Information). Meanwhile, the XPS measurements of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C composites were also performed after the cycling test, and the Co<span class="icomoon"></span>S bonds were still observed (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S22</a>, Supporting Information).</p>
         
         <p>Density functional theory (DFT) calculations were thus performed to uncover the internal mechanism of high-performance sodium storage of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C. The electronic structures of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and MoS<sub>2</sub>/C are presented in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0005">5g</a>, where the reduced bandgap is observed for SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C, which enhances the conductivity and accelerates the charge transfer. Furthermore, a much lower migration barrier of sodium atom on SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C (≈0.361&nbsp;eV) than that on MoS<sub>2</sub>/C (≈0.492&nbsp;eV) is obtained, as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0005">5h</a>, which manifests the fast reaction kinetics. As demonstrated in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0005">5i</a>, the adsorption energy of sodium atom on SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C is calculated to be −0.3153&nbsp;eV, much lower than that on MoS<sub>2</sub>/C (−0.7251&nbsp;eV), indicating that the sodium is more easily anchored on SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C than on MoS<sub>2</sub>/C, which contributes to the high sodium storage. In addition, the modulation of charge transfer by introducing Co single atom is further clarified by the Bader charge analysis (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S23</a>, Supporting Information). The detailed structure models of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and MoS<sub>2</sub>/C are shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S24</a> (Supporting Information).</p>
         
         <p>To evaluate the potential applications, the sodium-ion full cell was assembled using SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> (NVP) as the anode and cathode, respectively, as described in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adma202211690-fig-0006">6a</a>. The electrochemical properties of NVP cathode were firstly investigated and displayed in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S25</a> (Supporting Information). The galvanostatic charging/discharging curves of such a full cell for the first three cycles are revealed in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0006">6b</a>, indicative of its high stability. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0006">6c</a>, the sharp peaks at ≈2.26&nbsp;V in the cathodic sweep and ≈2.40&nbsp;V in the anodic sweep are obviously observed, suggesting the reversible conversion reaction. In addition, a relatively high specific capacity of ≈195.0 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> is obtained at 0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup> after 250 cycles (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0006">6d</a>). More importantly, as the current density reaches to 1 A g<sup>−1</sup>, the full cell represents outstanding long cyclic stability with a specific capacity of ≈125.0 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, even after 1200 cycles, the specific capacity is not declined (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0006">6e</a>). A light-emitting diode (LED) bulb is successfully lighted up by the assembled SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C//NVP full cell (inset of Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211690-fig-0006">6e</a>). The contrastive sodium-ion full cell performances of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C with other MoS<sub>2</sub>-based electrodes are shown in Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a> (Supporting Information). In addition, the energy density of such a full cell is calculated to be ≈228&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup>, which is higher than that of GeS<sub>2</sub>//Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>O<sub>2</sub>F (≈213&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup>),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211690-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0041_R_d21120032e1642" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - ACS Nano">41</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> SnSe<sub>2</sub>/N-doped porous carbon-fiber//Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>O<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub> (≈119&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup>),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211690-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0042_R_d21120032e1664" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - J. Power Sources">42</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and SnSe//Na<sub>0.67</sub>Ni<sub>0.41</sub>Mn<sub>0.72</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (≈141&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211690-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0043_R_d21120032e1681" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - Adv. Mater.">43</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adma202211690-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/36634625-981c-47c0-b646-595ac6f03f53/adma202211690-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/36634625-981c-47c0-b646-595ac6f03f53/adma202211690-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/57aa098b-3fee-4f78-97b1-45e1d37e10a9/adma202211690-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/36634625-981c-47c0-b646-595ac6f03f53/adma202211690-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma202211690-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.202211690" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Electrochemical performance of sodium-ion full cell composed of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C anode. a) Schematic illustration of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C//NVP full cell. b) Charging/discharging curves of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C//NVP full cell in the first three cycles at the current density of 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup>. c) CV curve of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C//NVP full cell at the second cycle. d,e) Cycling performances of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C//NVP full cell at the current densities of 0.5 and 1.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. Inset: Optical image of sodium-ion full cell lightening up a LED bulb.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
      </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adma202211690-sec-0030">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adma202211690-sec-0030-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>A facile and high-throughput diatomite-templated synthetic strategy is developed to produce SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C composites which are used as the sodium storage anodes. The introduction of Co single atom with unique coordination environment modifies the electronic structure of MoS<sub>2</sub>, optimizes the adsorption kinetics of intermediates, reduces the energy barrier of sodium ions diffusion, and boosts the charge transfer capacity. As expected, the excellent specific capacity, high rate performance, and long cyclic stability are obtained in the SIBs composed of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C anodes. Such results represent significant advance toward boosting the SIBs performances by introducing SACs on 2D TMDCs and enables the further practical applications.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adma202211690-sec-0040">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adma202211690-sec-0040-title">4 Experimental Section</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202211690-sec-0050">
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202211690-sec-0060">
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202211690-sec-0070">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adma202211690-sec-0070-title"> Synthesis of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C Composites</h4>
                  
                  <p>≈366&nbsp;mg C<sub>3</sub>H<sub>3</sub>N<sub>3</sub>S<sub>3</sub> powders were dispersed into ≈30&nbsp;mL deionized water and then stirred for ≈20 min at ≈50&nbsp;°C, followed by adding ≈2.2&nbsp;g diatomite powders into the suspension. Subsequently, ≈87&nbsp;mg Co(NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>2</sub>·6H<sub>2</sub>O, ≈228&nbsp;mg H<sub>3</sub>[P(Mo<sub>3</sub>O<sub>10</sub>)<sub>4</sub>], and ≈500&nbsp;mg C<sub>6</sub>H<sub>5</sub>Na<sub>3</sub>O<sub>7</sub> were dissolved into ≈10&nbsp;mL deionized water at ≈50 °C to achieve the clear solution and then added into the abovementioned suspension. Such mixtures were continuously stirred at ≈80&nbsp;°C until the solvent was completely evaporated. The obtained precursors were annealed at ≈600&nbsp;°C for ≈2 h. The diatomite templates and Co clusters were removed using the acid etching method, and then SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C composites were achieved. To further improve the crystalline quality, the obtained samples were annealed for ≈90 min in 5% H<sub>2</sub>/Ar atmosphere at ≈400&nbsp;°C. In addition, the bare MoS<sub>2</sub> was also synthesized using the same method without adding carbon sources.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202211690-sec-0080">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adma202211690-sec-0080-title"> Material Characterizations</h4>
                  
                  <p>The morphologies and atomic structures of the obtained samples were characterized by SEM (Hitachi S-4800, with the acceleration voltage of ≈5&nbsp;kV) and TEM (JEOL JEM-F200 and JEM-NEOARM, with the acceleration voltage of ≈200&nbsp;kV). The corresponding crystalline structures were analyzed by XRD (Rigaku, using Cu K<i>α</i> radiation in the 2<i>θ</i> range of 10°–90°) and Raman spectroscopy (Horiba, with the excitation light of ≈532&nbsp;nm). XPS (ESCALAB250Xi, with the excitation source of Al K<i>α</i>) measurements were performed to determine the effect of Co doping on the electronic structure of MoS<sub>2</sub>. The carbon content and loading capacity of Co single atom were characterized by TGA (Mettler-Toledo TGA/DSC 3+) and ICP-MS (Agilent 5110). EXAFS measurements were carried out at X-ray nanodiffraction (XND) beamline of Taiwan Photon Source (TPS, beamline 21A), National Synchrotron Radiation Research Center (NSRRC). This beamline adopted 4-bounce channel-cut Si(111) monochromator for mono-beam XND and X-ray absorption spectroscopy. The end-station equipped with three ionization chambers and Lytle/SDD detector after the focusing position of KB mirror for transmission and fluorescence mode X-ray absorption spectroscopy. The photon flux on the sample was ranged from 1 × 10<sup>11</sup>–3 × 10<sup>19</sup> photo s<sup>−1</sup> as the X-ray energy changing from ≈6 to ≈27&nbsp;keV. The obtained XAFS data were processed in Athena (version 0.9.26) for the background and pre-/post-edge lines calibrations. The Fourier transformed fitting was carried out in Artemis (version 0.9.26). For <i>k</i><sup>3</sup> weighting of commercial Co foil, the <i>k</i> and <i>R</i> ranges were set to be 3–14 Å<sup>−1</sup> and 1–3 Å, respectively. For <i>k</i><sup>3</sup> weighting of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C, the <i>k</i> and <i>R</i> ranges were set to be 3–12.5 Å<sup>−1</sup> and 1–3 Å, respectively. For WT analysis, the <i>χ</i>(k) exported from Athena was imported into the Hama Fortran code. The corresponding parameters were listed as follows: <i>R</i> and <i>k</i> ranges (1–4 Å and 0–12 Å<sup>−1</sup>), <i>k</i> weight (≈3).</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202211690-sec-0090">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adma202211690-sec-0090-title"> Electrochemical Measurements</h4>
                  
                  <p>The anodes were prepared by mixing active materials (≈80 wt%), acetylene black (≈10 wt%), and polyvinylidene fluoride binder (≈10 wt%) into a uniform slurry, and then pasted onto a Cu foil. The pellets were thoroughly dried under vacuum at ≈100&nbsp;°C for ≈12 h. The mass content of active material on each electrode (≈14&nbsp;mm in diameter) was set to be ≈0.8 to ≈1.2&nbsp;mg cm<sup>−2</sup>. The 2032-type coin cells were assembled in the Ar-filled glove box, with Na foil and Whatman glass fiber membrane as the counter electrode and separator, respectively. 1.0&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">m</span> NaPF<sub>6</sub> mixtures with ethylene carbonate/propylene carbonate (EC/PC, 1:1&nbsp;vol%) and ≈5 wt% fluoroethylene carbonate were used as the electrolyte. For the sodium-ion full cell, the cathode was prepared by mixing ≈80 wt% NVP, ≈10 wt% acetylene black, and ≈10 wt% polyvinylidene fluoride binder, which were coated on Al foil. The full cell was assembled using SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and NVP as the anode and cathode, respectively. The average mass loading of SA Co-MoS<sub>2</sub>/C was set to be ≈1.2&nbsp;mg cm<sup>−2</sup>, and the active materials mass ratio of anode/cathode was evaluated to be ≈1:5. The galvanostatic charging/discharging cycling and rate capability tests were performed on the LAND CT2001A multichannel battery testing system with a voltage window of ≈0.001 to ≈3.0&nbsp;V. The CV and EIS curves were recorded on a CHI 660D electrochemical workstation.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202211690-sec-0100">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adma202211690-sec-0100-title"> Computational Methods</h4>
                  
                  <p>The Vienna Ab Initio Package (VASP) was used to perform the DFT calculations<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211690-bib-0044" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0044_R_d21120032e1881" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 44 - Phys. Rev. B">44</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> within the generalized gradient approximation (GGA) using the Perdew–Burke–Enzerhof (PBE) formulation.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211690-bib-0045" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0045_R_d21120032e1886" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 45 - Phys. Rev. Lett.">45</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The projected augmented wave (PAW) potentials were applied to describe the ionic cores, and the valence electrons were considered using a plane wave basis set with a kinetic energy cutoff of 450&nbsp;eV. The partial occupancies of Kohn–Sham orbitals were allowed using the Gaussian smearing method with a width of 0.05&nbsp;eV. The electronic energy was considered self-consistent as the energy change was smaller than 10<sup>−6</sup>&nbsp;eV. A geometry optimization was considered convergent when the force change was smaller than 0.03&nbsp;eV Å<sup>−1</sup>. The Grimme's DFT-D3 methodology was used to describe the dispersion interactions. The vacuum spacing perpendicular to the plane was set to be 20 Å. The Brillouin zone integral utilized the surfaces structures of 3 × 3 × 1 Monkhorst–Pack <i>K</i> point sampling. The climbing image-nudged elastic band (CI-NEB) method was employed to calculate the Na<sup>+</sup> ions migration barrier.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211690-bib-0046" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211690-bib-0046_R_d21120032e1900" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 46 - J. Chem. Phys.">46</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
                  </section>
               </section>
            </section>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">

                  <li data-bib-id="adma202211690-bib-0004"><span class="bullet">4</span><span class="author">J.-Y. Hwang</span>, <span class="author">S.-T. Myung</span>, <span class="author">Y.-K.
